I watched the video and made this recipe before reading the reviews.  I wouldn't have tried it after reading all the negative comments, but I'm so glad I did.  I made this for company and we all loved it!  I did have to bake longer than 35 mins (probably closer to 50) and the croutons got very crunchy on top but it was fantastic.  My husband took leftovers to work and many colleagues asked for the recipe because it smelled so good! I've very rarely make Chicken Parmesan because of the time it takes to prepare, but this will be one of my regulars.

text:
First, let me say that I followed the directions as written for the most part.  I only had half the amount of mozzarella on hand, I forgot the red pepper flake and I used chicken tenders instead of breasts.  Very, very good recipe.  I only have a couple of suggestions.  First, use chicken tenders, they cook faster and they're easier to portion.  Second, I will grind up the croutons next time and add them on top of the cheese.  I could probably use bread crumbs for that, but I like the buttery taste that the croutons give.  I wasn't missing the red pepper flake that I left out.  I was also perfectly happy with half the amount of mozzarella, and I'm a cheeseaholic.  Also, I used a variety of our store's brand of pasta sauce (because it's really, really good).  Thanks Chef John for a great recipe I will use again!

text:
Yum! With a little tweaking, you can make this super fast and easy without having to thaw your chicken breasts first. What I did was coat the bottom of the pan with sauce, place the frozen chicken on top, then cover with the rest of the sauce and spices. Baked for about 45 minutes, added the cheese/breadcrumbs and let that sit under the broiler to crisp and brown up for a couple minutes, and viola! Perfectly moist, flavorful chicken and no thawing required! Lovely recipe.

This is a definite keeper! WOW! I sprayed my glass 9x13 dish with Pam, trimmed the fat from 6 chicken breats and laid them flat, sprinkled them with garlic powder, red pepper and poultry seasoning.  I covered them with one jar of Prego Light spaghetti sauce and a slice of mozarella cheese over each breast.  Topped that with crushed up garlic croutons and some parmesan cheese.  Cooked it at 350, uncovered for 50 minutes.  DELICIOUS!!

text:
After reading the reviews, *** I sliced the breasts in half lengthwise so they were thinner.*** They cooked up fine.  I used 3 cloves of garlic, quite a hefty pinch of pepper flakes, and a nice spaghetti sauce that my family likes. It was delicious! It is best straight from the oven so the topping will be crunchy - microwaving leftovers does not work. The crouton topping is very hearty and NOT for weight watchers... a lot of carbs... may try again without the topping to save some carbs and calories. Also, adding all the cheese at the beginning is not what I do - I cook the chicken most of the way through before adding the cheese... otherwise, it turns brown from overcooking. But the dish was tasty, and easy to make.

text:
Yum! My hubs and I thought this was pretty good. While not "traditional," this is perfect for a quick weeknight meal. Having said this, only a few tweaks are required to take this from good to GREAT! Because I had extra time on my hands (and because I viewed John's video FIRST), I browned my chicken in a T of EVOO until browned on both sides. I then poured the pan juices over my chicken as suggested. I used chicken cutlets instead of breasts (I feared they'd cook unevenly otherwise) and this caused my chicken to DRY out! I should have known better.... Thin cutlets cook quickly! I have a few suggestions for those wanting to give John's recipe a try. First, DO NOT pan fry your chicken (as per Chef John's video). This step is totally unnecessary, IMHO. Second, add the basil (if it's in season). It definitely kicks this up a notch. Finally, use smallish sized croutons. I purchased Marzetti brand garlic & onion croutons and although tasty, they were very LARGE. I had a difficult time covering them (with cheese) and the ones that were exposed got a little too brown for my liking. :( I suggest that you semi-crush your croutons to avoid this (and cover your casserole with foil for at least HALF of the time it is in the oven). With these changes, your recipe will become a regular staple at my house. Thaks for sharing, Chef John! :-)

text:
I was really nervous to try this recipe, based on all the negative reviews. I decided to cut the recipe down to 4 servings, just in case it was terrible. Too bad, too, because this recipe is delicious! When I was heating up our leftovers today, my husband exclaimed, "my mouth is watering!" 

NOTE TO GLUTEN-FREE COOKS: I used Glutino brand gluten-free "bread sticks" and crumbled them on top, instead of croutons. I also served it on a bed of quinoa pasta crumbles (because let's face it, quinoa pasta never holds together) with butter, salt and pepper. Turned out great!

I have no idea how much or how little cheese, sauce or basil (dried) I used. I just eyeballed it. I used a bit more garlic than the recipe asked for because my husband and I both love it. Also, I ended up baking it for about 40-45 minutes (and I only used 4 halves). GREAT recipe! We'll definitely be having this again.

text:
Let me preface this by saying that I did change the method in which this recipe was put together, but did not alter any of the ingredients or quantities. The bad reviews for this made me not want to try it, but I thought I would give it a chance anyway.

It seemed odd to me to layer the bottom of the baking dish with garlic, oil and red pepper flakes so instead I sliced the chicken breast into 1" strips and browned them in the olive oil along with the garlic. I sprayed the baking dish with Pam and then added the chicken/garlic mix and then followed the recipe as written. I also crushed the croutons into pieces slightly larger then crumbs.

The flavor was phenomenal, however, I also used homemade spaghetti meat sauce in place of the marinara, which may have enhanced the flavor as well.

text:
I made this recipe as shown and found it to be a fast and easy fix. This recipe has potential but I would make a few changes the next time I make it. First add some bread crumbs to the bottom of the casserole. It was a little soupy on the bottom so this should soak up liquid better. Second, add 1/2 the marinara over the chicken, add the croutons, then cover with the rest of the sauce and top with cheese. Croutons are already dry and baking them on top with half the cheese made them even harder. Covering with a little sauce and cheese will allow the croutons to soften a little and give it just the right crisp/tender texture you want in a good chicken parmesan.

I almost didn't make this based on other reviews, were my croutons going to be soggy were they going to be like rocks??  They were awesome...exactly as promised...soaked in sauce on the bottom and cheesy crunchy on the top.  Mmmm Mmmmm Good!  I made exactly as stated (watching the video).  I browned the chicken first.  Deglazed the pan with a little white wine and poured it over the chicken.  I'm not really sure what a "good" crouton is.  I usually make my own croutons but I didn't think they would work in this since I usually like them chewy crisp so I bought Rothbury Farm Italian Style croutons and they were fabulous in this dish. Oh, I also used the recipe from this site "The Best Marinara Sauce Yet"  as my marinara sauce.  So glad I did.  I cooked my chicken for 40 minutes and should have stuck with 35 and I will next time. Thank you Chef John for another winner recipe.

text:
This was very good!  Hubs and I both really enjoyed it.  I deviated just a bit, but not much.  First I pounded my chicken to about 1/2" so it would cook more evenly.  I skipped the oil and sprayed my pan with non-stick cooking spray, then sprinkled in the crushed red pepper flakes.  Rather than put the garlic in the pan, I put it in my sauce, which was a spaghetti sauce.  Topped the chicken with the sauce and sprinkled on the fresh basil and the first layer of both mozzarella (mine was actually a mozzarella/provolone blend) and parmesan cheeses, just eyeballing the amounts of cheeses.  At this point I covered and refrigerated it until dinnertime.   When I was ready to bake this, I uncovered it and topped it with my own homemade croutons and the remaining cheeses.  I baked this for about 40 minutes.  Remember if your croutons begin to brown too quickly, lay a piece of foil over the dish and continue baking.  Not only was this very tasty, but a snap to put together.  Weâ€™ll be making this one again!

This is the dish I serve when I have company over for supper. Super easy casserole and everyone loves it!
My suggestion would be to use 2 jars of marinara sauce which is about 3 1/2 to 4 cups of marinara and 2 bags of crutons I don't find that one bag is enough! This is an interesting and tasty recipe, but certainly not chicken Parmesan as you expect it to be.  I prepared the dish exactly as written, except I salt & peppered both sides of the breasts b/4 putting in the baking dish. I put it in the oven 30 minutes earlier anticipating the extra cooking time so many reviewers said was needed.  As it turned out, the meat was done in 35 minutes as the recipe stated. Perhaps this was because I made sure the chicken was at room temperature before cooking it. If prepared right out of the fridge, cooking time will be significantly longer. At any rate, I will make this again for variety, but if I'm in the mood for chicken Parmesan, I'll stick to my traditional recipe.

text:
I love Chef John's recipes! I make his traditional chicken parmesan recipe all the time so I was keen to try this because it looked so easy. 
 
I was so glad I decided to try this recipe on a day that the plumbing in my kitchen went haywire, it was so easy to put together and I dirtied almost no pots and pans in the process.
 
I made a few changes based on the reviews: I used thin sliced breasts and salt and peppered the chicken before I slightly seared them on the stove. I melted a bit of butter and added it to the wine to deglaze the pan and poured it over the chicken before topping it with the sauce. I used Bertolli tomato and basil pasta sauce. I didn't feel like mincing fresh garlic so I used dried minced but I did use the fresh basil. I used some brand of croutons made from Texas toast and tried to break them up into smaller pieces. I added a bit to the bottom of the dish with a few spoon fulls of sauce before adding the chicken. I added some cracked black pepper on top of  the cheese before the croutons went on and I added a bit of olive oil on top of the croutons before the last layer of cheese. I covered and baked for about 30 min then 10 uncovered.

 It came out perfect!! Super tasty and an excellent substitute for traditional chicken parmesan without all the fuss of breading the chicken first.

Thanks Chef John!

This was a very good Emergency Dinner.  I had everything on hand.  Son wiped out on skateboard, possible elbow fracture.  Dr. won't have report back until after weekend.  Didn't want to drag said son all over the grocery store with a swollen arm in a sling.  Raided my freezer and pantry.  Followed recipe and noted reviews that said to season and brown the chicken first and crush the croutons.  Best Husband Ever was coming home from a business trip, so I wanted a hot, home cooked meal on the table that was also easy for me.  Everyone loved it.  Used Trader Joe's Tuscan Marinara in the 14oz can which was the perfect amount and for sauce from a can, it rates highly in my book.  Best Husband Ever said I could make this anytime.  And, I like the fact it's not fried.  The cheese did brown quickly on the top, so keep an eye out and tent with foil as soon as it's browned to your liking - I almost overshot the runway on that step.  The crushed red pepper flakes and garlic on the bottom is a brilliant idea - added just the right kick without being too much for my 11 year old.  Not necessarily a dish I would choose for a dinner party, but it's definitely a keeper for a weeknight, quick, yummy dish.  We skipped doing any pasta with it and no one missed it - the crouton topping does that job just fine for us.

For the amount of time and effort, this meal *really* gets the job done.  Chicken Parmesan isn't something I would order dining out so this dish isn't anything unique.  I'm not even a huge fan of "Italian" cuisine.  However, like I said, for the amount of effort it is certainly tasty and gets the job done and in a nutritious way.  So that's why I give it 5 stars.

The tomato sauce I used was flavored with garlic and basil so I was fine using dried basil.  I used a square glass baking dish and used only 4 breasts, perfect size for my family.  It all turned out great.

This is a recipe I will definitely be able to make from memory.  So while I'm at the grocery store fretting about dinner, I can easily remember all the ingredients and whip it up in no time.

text:
Love this easy "Chicken Parmesan" styled casserole. I've made this exactly according to directions(and it's awesome) and I've also altered it many times. I find now when I make it, I brown the outside of the chicken breasts first in a frying pan in some oil to lower the cooking time in the oven. I also never have fresh basil in the house so I use the dried stuff.  I probably use way more cheese than the recipe calls for and probably double the pasta sauce.  It's super easy to make and the croutons give a good crunch rather than having the breaded coating on the outside. I love serving this over rice as I'm not a huge pasta fan. I wouldn't say it would replace my traditional styled chicken Parmesan recipe but I've definitely made this way more times than the old recipe since it's convenient and tastes great.

I made this pretty much according to the recipe. I had chicken from Sam's Club which are large, so sliced them into 2, lengthwise. I used more cheese, pepper flakes, seasoning, marinara and croutons than called for. It was extremely well received and the family made me promise to make it again soon. I served it with linguine.  Having read about the problem with reheating, I cut the leftovers into chunks, including the cheese and croutons and then mixed it into a box of newly made linguine. I added more marinara so it stayed somewhat wet in the reheating. It was just as good as the original when reheated this way. Thanks for a great recipe!

This was easy to throw together and tasty. Based on the reviews I made just a few small changes in the way I combined the ingredients. 

I cut the chicken breasts in half and browned them with the garlic, basil and some dried minced onion. I put a layer of sauce on the bottom of the baking dish before adding the chicken as well. I deglazed the pan with a jar of marinara before topping the chicken. Otherwise I followed the recipe exactly. Only other change was that I "semi" crushed the croutons, which I would definitely recommend, but that could just be a matter of personal taste :)

I will make this again!

text:
First time I made this recipe exactly as described, but found it did need just a lil tweaking to our likings...  First thing I did was brown the chicken in some olive oil & garlic b4 I put in the 9x13" greased tin foil lined pan.   Then I put  bout 1/2 cup of sauce in bottom of pan as described w/red pepper flakes, garlic salt & some Italian seasoning... I sprinkled cut up chicken (in about 5" chunks) over that, then poured the rest of the bottled Bertolli pasta sauce,  sprinkled bout 1Tbs. of  Basil (we luv the taste of basil!), 1/2 tsp of garlic powder & 1cup of  lil bit crushed up  Panko bread crumbs.  Then..added .the 2 cheeses... I bake it  covered w/foil for about 45min.   Then, took foil off & let it brown about 3 min under the broiler.  Very good flavor throughout the chicken & moist & tender.  Everyone really liked it.... A LOT!!!

This recipe was delicious, and a smashing hit with the family. I used Wildtree's Garlic Grapeseed Oil both in the skillet to brown my chicken, and in the bottom of the casserole dish. I also deglazed (sp?) the pan as Chef John's video suggested. I highly recommend that step! It did take longer to cook than I expected, and I did cover it about halfway through with foil so that my croutons and cheese wouldn't get too crisp, but I had a couple thicker cuts of chicken that I didn't sear for long enough in the skillet, so I know what to change next time to make it a bit faster. I served it over linguine tossed in the homemade Alfredo sauce that we always make at home (a household favorite). I will definitely make this recipe again and again. You rock, Chef John! My husband and I are big fans! :)

I made this last night as a last minute put-it-together kind of meal. My 9 year old had her very Italian BFF over for dinner so I was a little nervous because that age can be brutally honest. Loved it for how stupid simple it was with all ingredients I always have on hand.  I had the larger frozen chicken breasts but did cut them in half and they baked in about 35-40 minutes. Kids cleaned their plates and that's worth 5 stars in itself!!

text:
This was easy to throw together and delicious.  I didn't use the pepper flakes (don't like) or the basil (didn't have) and I messed up the order of the cheese and sauce layers, but this recipe is pretty much goof proof and very forgiving. Forget the marinara and just use whatever favorite flavor of sauce in a jar you have on hand. Adjust your cooking time to the size of your chicken breasts, and if you cook too long, the croutons just get more crunchy. Don't expect "gourmet", just tasty, fast, and only one dirty dish.

text:
This was actually a 3.5 star dish for me but since I think that was due to my own variations I'm giving it 4 stars.  This seems more like a "deconstructed chicken parmesan" than a true chicken parm, particularly since the chicken was not breaded and browned before baking.  But it sounded tasty enough to give it a go.  Flavor-wise it's a solid 4 stars.  I think thatwill have a lot to do with whatever marinara/red sauce you choose since that's where the main flavor punch comes from.  I used thin-sliced chicken breasts since that's what I had on hand and they were kind of lost amidst the sauce/cheese/croutons.  My mistake.  Next time I'll use larger chicken breasts.  Also, I chose to top everything off with a bit more sauce befor epopping it in the oven.  Unfortunately that made for more soggy/less crunchy croutons.  But again, that was *my* mistake.  One I won't make again.  The flavor was great, though, so I'll definitely try this again.

text:
I made this for dinner tonight and it was very good. I should have read the reviews before cooking though. When I took it out of the oven after 35 minutes, the top was very brown but the minute I put the chicken on the plate, I could tell it was not done. I covered the dish with foil and put it back in the oven for 15 more minutes. The next time I make it I will either slice the breasts thinner or use tenders as others have recommended. Also, I think I will crunch up the croutons a little. I used large croutons and they got very crunchy. I think the type of sauce you use makes all the difference in the taste - be sure it is a sauce that you and your family like. All in all, it is a wonderful recipe and I will definitely make it again!

text:
Used thin chicken breasts and bread crumbs as this is what I had on hand, no red pepper flakes as we don't care for that kind of heat.  Result is.....meh.  I see why you would use croutons, but you will definitely want to crush them a bit.  Breadcrumbs are mushy and lost in between cheeses.  Next time, I would use spiced panko crumbs.  No need to "sandwich" the crumbs with cheese either.  Cheese first, crumbs on top.  Cooked 20 minutes with lid, 15 w/o.  Even so, recipe is still meh.  No pizazz, but edible.  If I do again, I will use panko, with pepper jack cheese.  BTW, served on buttered wheat spaghetti with chopped spinach mixed in.

text:
This was a nice dish but I made two crucial mistakes. I used chicken breasts that were just too plump. Choose ones that are smaller. The second mistake I made was using croutons that were too large and Chef John cautions against this in the video version of this recipe. Smaller croutons disperse better into the sauce and crisp up nicely while the larger ones tend to stick out of the sauce more and harden and burn. This would have been a great dish if I hadn't made those mistakes. You can always count on Chef John to introduce us to great dishes. Thank you Chef John.

text:
I have made this 3 times now. It's a great casserole to make for a large group, since traditional chicken Parmesan would be too time consuming to make. My guests loved it!  I followed the recipe exactly, except that I cut my large chicken Breasts in half. That way, my guests had the option of taking a small portion or a larger one. The first time I made it, the top got a bit too dark and crunchy. The subsequent times, I loosely covered the pan with foil, and removed the foil for the last 10-15 minutes to prevent overcooking the cheese and croutons on the top. I serve this with pene or another pasta.

city:
None
region:
None
country:
None
text:
I used shortcuts.  I used 5 frozen chicken patties from Costco (defrosted and cut in chunks).  Put in a 8x8 pan (lightly greased), chicken chunks, poured jarred pasta sauce on chunks and coated, used a bag of shredded mozzarella cheese (2cups).  In a separate bowl,  I took about a cup of croutons, crushed them and added 1/4 c. of bread crumbs, added 2 tbs of melted butter, mixed well.  Spread topping on top of chicken and cheese sprinkled with 1/4 c. Parmesan cheese.  Cook at 350 degree oven for about 40 mins.  I suggest a bigger pan (lightly greased), cover with foil and remove last 10 mins of cooking time.  Overall, it was easy, delicious and fast.  Served with garlic bread and salad.

After reading a few reviews, I browned the chicken and did not use the mega-breasts sold; cut them in half.  I used the marinara as a base, no spray.  The  garlic and hot peppers went on the chicken instead of at the bottom of the pan.  Crushed the croutons.  Covered during the baked and then took off to brown cheese/croutons.  Use real cheese - it makes a difference and this is a keeper!

region:
None
country:
None
text:
I have made this dish twice already. I love how simple it is. I thin-slice the chicken breast and lay them on a bed of basil-tomato sauce over olive oil, fresh minced garlic, and then add a can of Italian style diced tomatos. Next I add a nice thick tomato-basi marinara sauce. The thin-sliced chicken makes the whole dish cook a bit faster and it gives the chicken more flavor. After I add the cheese, I top it all off with homemade croutons or add small cubes of French or hoagie bread. They toast nice on top of the cheese. Lastly, I sprinkle the top with more basil and a bit more pepper flakes. Me and my husband love this dish, and it makes superb leftovers.

text:
This is amazing and so good.  My family loves Italian but the from scratch recipes, ( that are the best ), take a lot of time. When I came across this recipe I knew it was going to be a winner at our table. All that great Italian taste and so little work! ---- I just tweaked it a little----
*** Be sure to cover with a tent of foil until last 15 minutes of cooking and my total cook time was 50 minutes, I cooked my chicken breast first, then followed the recipe from there. I did add one forth of a cup of chopped onion. (I add onion to everything). I believe sauteing the chicken in olive oil with the onion and garlic made it so nice! Also with the leftovers the next day I cooked a little pasta and served the casserole on top, ( to make it go further). 
***Update to my review: I forgot to mention that after I cooked the chicken, I diced it into about inch sized pieces. I found it was easier to serve that way. If you want to serve a whole half piece to each person then don't cut up chicken, but for kids this worked better for me.

text:
I changed the recipe up a little bit since I use this as a make ahead meal. I use chicken breast tenderloin since it is easier to cook all the way through. I use olive oil, garlic paste, basil paste and the red pepper flake to coat the bottom of the pan and it infuses the chicken with those flavors. I hedge my bets a little bit and use a pre-made marinara sauce that is tomato and basil. I add oregano on top of the marinara sauce to give it an extra Italian flavor. This is very easy and it comes out moist and with incredible flavors. BTW, it freezes well too.

text:
Surprisingly good! Instead of the fresh basil, I used dried Italian seasoning. I used jarred sauce and lightly seasoned the chicken with garlic and onion powders, as well as salt and pepper. Then I cooked it with tin foil over the top (to speed up cooking) for 30 mins. I then added pre-shredded cheeses, a can of sliced black olives and topped with a bag of croutons,  then I baked it for an additional 15. I turned the oven off, and switched over to the broil setting and broiled the top for about 4 mins. I can't believe how easy this was, and really good! I would eat this on the regular, thanks!

text:
My husband kept telling how good this meal was and I' m so pleased with the ease of preparation.  I made a couple of minor changes. First I sprayed the bottom of my glass baking dish with Pam to cut down on fat, and sprinkled  2 cloves of crushed garlic and about 1/4 tsp aground red  pepper on the bottom of the dish. Next I laid my six chicken breasts on top (next time I'd definitely slice them in half length wise, or better yet slice them into tenders ), followed by a 24 oz. can of traditional Hunts spaghetti sauce. I then sprinkled about 1/8 c. Fresh parsley and 1/8 c. fresh basil. Next put 1/2 the cheeses. Because Im gluten free I coarsely crushed some almond rice crackers on top, sprayed them with Pam and sprinkled with about 1/8 t garlic powder. Then the rest of the cheeses. I baked them  for 20 minutes, covered them with foil and baked again for 20 more minutes.  Excellent and easy. Next time I'll add more marinara and serve it on spaghetti. Thanks for the recipe!

text:
I follow the recipe preaty close but I add 1/8 inch slices of eggplant to mine. I will wrap the chicken into a large slice or 2 of rinsed eggplant (slice the eggplant at a 1/8 " thickness on a Madeleine, place the eggplant in a colander and sprinkle with sea salt and let sit in the sink to drain and leach the moisture for about 30 to 40 minutes, then rinse the salt off  the eggplant and pat it all dry on thick absorbent paper towels.

next I sprayed the bottom of the baking dish with olive oil pam, then added my favorite spaghetti sauce, for me garlic and basil.

I add the chicken thighs and breast to a large cast-iron skillet with 1st press olive oil and 6 large clove of roasted garlic, {I always roast off 4 to 6 LARGE whole garlics wraped in tin foil sprayed with a little pam olive oil and some course sea salt, like pink a Himalayan, or a Flure De Lure...is how the last is speeled I hope it's in French and I'm jusy and odd hay seed ??. you want to crisp in the natural juices with a high hot burner setting...be very careful of the grease spray back.
once you have finnished the chicken place on the paper towel re-pat to remove excess oil & grease.

place chicken into the backing dishadd chicken broth to the dish to come up on the chicken about1/4 of the way.
top with a mozzarella and parmesan, a little care free application of Panko bread crumbs mixed with chopped fresh parsley and parmesan cheese and a cool crisp garden salad, and perhaps a cauliflower and broccoli potatoes

text:
Pretty good. I followed the recipe exactly, except that I pounded out the thick ends of the chicken breasts a bit, and then cut each piece into two for more even cooking (and to make smaller portions since we have kids). It smelled freaking amazing in the oven while it baked! I let it bake 40 minutes and the chicken was done perfectly. It tasted great. Only problem was that I ended up with a lot of liquid at the bottom of the pan for some reason. So I used a slotted spoon to dish it out and it wasn't too much of a problem. Everybody quite liked it. Served over fettuccine with a big salad. I suggest putting extra marinara sauce on the table for spooning, if serving with pasta, as the casserole doesn't yield much sauce.

Turned out great -- chicken was perfectly tender...entire dish was extremely flavorful. I doubled the recipe (we had guests), and while the fresh dish had exactly the right 'bread crunch' the crouton bits swelled considerably in the leftovers. Next go 'round I will probably reduce the croutons and cheese by 1/3 each (especially if cooking with leftovers in mind). Guests also seemed to prefer a tablespoon of fresh marina on each serving (diced tomatoes, olive oil, black pepper, fresh basil, dried oregano...left to simmer while main dish baked).

My kids ate all of this, amazing. Did not watch the video first, though I probably would have made the same adjustments even if I had.  Proportions weren't exact (more chicken in total and a mishap resulted in too much red pepper), but it was still good. I used thin cut chicken breasts, fat free mozzarella, and Romano cheese. I did not pre-fry the chicken, and the whole casserole was juicier but still ok. I double layered the chicken in a 9x13 and they were a little hard to get out individually.  Will definitely make this again (likely will leave out the red pepper altogether) because it was good and super easy.

It was really good!  I made by the directions with minor changes.  It will only be as good as the sauce and croutons you use.  I used Vitoria Tomato Basil premium sauce and a bag of Olive Garden Garlic and Romano croutons.  The only change I made was to use boneless chicken thighs, because I prefer them.  I put a thin layer of sauce on the bottom.  I did brown the chicken and deglaze the pan as in the video with Marsala wine and used sliced fresh mozzarella and Kraft shredded Italian cheese blend.  I pushed several croutons down into the sauce and broke up the rest used on top and patted them down.  Served it over some angel hair pasta.  I will definitely make again.

I followed this recipe as given except for using spaghetti sauce rather than marinara (and using about 1/3 more than the recipe called for so I could use up the jar); and using chicken tenderloins rather than chicken breasts.

I watched the video first, and sautÃ©ed my chicken first like the video showed. But if I'd seen the video before buying the ingredients, I'd have looked for a different recipe because sauteeing is an extra step that makes it less quick and convenient. Sauteeing was NOT mentioned in the written recipe, which I found shoddy. Nearly 800 reviews and that discrepancy hasn't been noticed and corrected?!

It was an "okay" dish, but my family usually gobbles up seconds and they did not refill their plates. . The croutons seemed not the best choice. Just kind of fattening and weird, not adding any great pleasing crunch. Why not instead use a starch like rice, noodles, or potatoes to make it more of a full meal casserole instead? Better yet, include a green vegetable too and have a whole meal in one pan for your trouble. I'd overlook that if it was an exceptional recipe but it was not.

text:
Fairly easy and a nice change to pasta and sauce. Made a half recipe. Put tomato and basil Classico sauce on bottom of pan. Defrosted 2-3 chicken breasts,  sliced in half (thin way), and put on top of sauce. Generously sprinkled spices on top of chicken (red pepper flakes, poultry seasoning, garlic powder and basil).  Then pour rest of sauce on top of chicken. Baked at 350 for about 50 mins. Then put mozzarella and shredded parmesan cheese on top, along with broken up croutons (add extra croutons). Broil for 1-2 minutes. Can serve alone or with pasta. If eating with pasta, use extra sauce.

This turned out pretty well.  The rating is due to a lack of crunchiness in the topping, but perhaps if I cooked it longer the croutons would have been crunchy.  I made a few changes--I only used 5 chicken breasts (and still fed myself and 6 kids).  I skipped the red pepper flakes, opting for ground black pepper.  There was no fresh basil so I had to make do with dried and also added some Italian seasoning.  I did crush the croutons in a bag before sprinkling on the top.  I only cooked this for 40 min since I had sliced the chicken in to strips.  We all enjoyed it and yes, I would make it again.

atbarber

city:
None
region:
None
country:
None
text:
I reduced the number of servings as I was only using 2 chicken breasts. I pounded the chicken so it was of even thickness (about 1/2 inch).  As shown in the video, I did lightly brown the chicken that had been seasoned with salt and pepper and a little crushed red pepper,  in a little olive oil.  I added a little olive oil mixed with a small amount of the bottled organic pasta sauce, then placed the chicken pieces on top.  Spooned some of the sauce on each piece of chicken, then topped with some chopped fresh basil, oregano and minced garlic.  Added some of both cheeses, then placed in the pre-heated oven covered for 20 minutes.   Took it out of the oven, added some homemade garlic herb croutons (small sized) and topped with the remaining cheese.   Baked for an additional 15 minutes and until the cheese was melted and slightly browned.

I served this with a side dish of zucchini, onion, garlic and pasta sauce that had been simmered until the zucchini was crisp tender.

I enjoyed the flavors but thought the texture of the croutons with the chicken was off.  I would have preferred it if I had crushed the croutons instead of leaving them whole even though they were small.

text:
This is one of our new favorites. I scaled down the recipe to 2 servings (but used a whole clove of garlic), used my own leftover spaghetti sauce from the night before and the Italian croutons I had on hand.

EDIT for Novice cooking friends: I didn't measure cheese or time it. I used what I knew we'd like like and took it out when it began to brown.  I put more of the cheese on the chicken layer than the crouton layer, so that the croutons would have more crunch. I think the poor reviews came from people watching the video and trying to replicate everything so exactly.

text:
This is the perfect super-easy replacement for traditional chicken parmesan.  The red pepper flakes add a spicy bite to each mouthful, while the garlic croutons give intermittent mouthfuls of savory crunch and sauce-drenched deliciousness.   I chose to slice my chicken breasts into tenderloin-sized pieces to allow for smaller servings to be taken.  The combination of cheeses layered between the chicken and croutons and for the topping was the perfect way to meld the whole dish into a hearty, satisfying main course that is quick to put together and got a "thumbs up" from everyone.  Paired with a green salad, this makes a great option for a week-night dinner.

This turned out much better than I thought it would!  After reading other reviews, I also put some of the marinara on the bottom of the dish, rather than the garlic.  I put the chicken down and seasoned with red pepper flakes and garlic, then layered the marinara and mozzarella.  I crushed up the croutons which made it easier to cover the dish and covered it with foil for the first 25 min of baking.  This took about 50 min to cook rather than 35 min but my chicken was fairly thick.  Delicious!

text:
One of hubby's favorite meals!  I didn't change ingredients, but did change the method a little.  However, I only use 3 chicken breasts.   I cube the chicken.  I follow directions up to the sauce and first layer of cheeses, then bake for 20 minutes.  If it seems watery, I remove the water with my turkey baster.  I then put on the croutons, and the remaining cheese.  This keeps the croutons from getting soggy. Then bake another 15 minutes.

text:
Very easy to make and tasted delicious -- would make a couple of changes next time.  I would crush up the croutons a bit and sprinkle a few table spoons of sauce over them before adding the last of cheese.  The croutons were super crunchy and chunky . . .this would have been a bit more parm like and easier to eat if the croutons were smaller and some were softer.  I used 1lb of chicken breast tenders, a jar of Paul Newman plain marinara, Italian seasoned croutons, and dried basil  . . . tasted great.  Because I used tenders . . . I only needed to bake for 35 minutes.  I also added a bit of garlic powder, pepper and salt to the tenders before adding sauce.   Looking forward to making again.

text:
Perfection!! I used a tuscan flavored olive oil in the bottom. I used a whole jar of sauce - why not - you only live once! I seasoned the chicken on the one side before I poured on the sauce. I sprinkled the chicken with dried oregano, dried basil and garlic salt. I didn't have any fresh basil. Those spices really added a depth of flavor. Everything else was the same, except for one more sprinkle of dried oregano across the top cheese layer. We fell in love! Important to not use super fat breasts - I used regular-sized breasts. Made a big difference in the final product. If your breast are huge (tee hee), you might want to cut them in half to make them skinnier. Enjoy!

text:
My family and i loved this recipe! I did make a couple of tweeks though.........i sprayed the baking dish with PAM instead of using oil and i sprinkled it with garlic powder instead of the chopped garlic (mostly cause i was too lazy that day to chop garlic!). I had to bake it for about 45 mins for the chicken to be done and by then the cheese was really hard and the croutons had started to burn but it still had an awesome flavor.  When i make this again (and i DEFINITELY will) before i add the cheese and croutons i will bake the dish about half way then add the cheese and croutons. All in all........awesome recipe and super quick to make!!

text:
Wonderful!  I did use some tips from other reviewers, sliced the breasts across as these were very large, then I marinated them in a mix of basil infused EVOO Italian seasoning and balsamic vinegar.  Didn't bother to seer them.  Didn't have the red pepper flakes but I added some minced roasted garlic on top of the prepared glass pan before adding a little sauce, then the chicken, sauce, a bit of smoked paprika, the cheeses.  I typically buy the large restaurant size croutons, so I did use a rolling pin to crush them down in size while still leaving chunks.  I decided to use convection baking until the sauce was bubbling, added the remaining cheeses and baked another 10 minutes.  Total baking time was 30 min.  My husband kept asking how long until dinner as he said it smelled GREAT!  This was SO moist and flavorful, I will use again for us, but it's going to be a company dish as well!  THANKS Chef John, and other reviewers!

text:
This is seriously so simple. I even had to re-read the recipe to make sure I had not forgotten any steps because it was that simple. There is a new video out from Chef John that updates this recipe a teeny bit which includes cooking the chicken for a few minutes on both sides to get a yummy golden crust. I was lazy and didn't feel like doing that, so I threw the breasts in raw. I used canned tomato sauce (again, lazy), and didn't have any fresh basil, so I used basil olive oil across the bottom of the casserole dish as well as drizzled a little across the top of the chicken before spreading the tomato sauce. I did season the chicken breasts with salt, pepper and a little bit of garlic powder before dousing them in tomato sauce, but the rest of the recipe stayed true (with the exception of the missing basil). Mine cooked for about 50 minutes and it was perfectly done. One dish wonder. Who would have thought to use croutons for the "breading?" Chef John. My husband said "this is amazing." In our house, nothing exceeds "pretty good." This will most definitely be going into the regular rotation in our house!

text:
made this last night for dinner & eating leftovers right now for lunch.  Warmed up very good.  I used a whole Sam's size bag of chicken tenderloins thawed.Spread some spaghetti sauce on bottom of pan (will use aluminum foil next time) and poured chicken over top.  Sprinkled with garlic powder & basil then poured rest of sauce on top.  I used almost a whole big jar of sauce and we actually had to add more to our spaghetti on the side (I'm assuming it's bc I used way more chicken).  I covered with cheese & Parmesan and croutons (which I broke in half) & then more cheese.  Didn't quite use the whole bag of cheese.  Cooked about 35 min covered then broiled a few minutes at the end (I was worried about the croutons burning as others mentioned).  Everything was delicious - 13 yr old loved it.  Served with zoodles for adults (spiralized zuchinni  "noodles") & spaghetti for the kiddos

text:
This is good for a weeknight dinner as it comes together fast. I seasoned the chicken with black pepper, garlic powder, onion powder, basil and oregano then seared for a couple minutes on each side. I then proceeded with the sauce, parmesan cheese, Italian cheese blend and croutons, I covered with foil so the croutons would not be rock hard. I served with vermicilli that I tossed with butter, garlic and parmesan cheese and a salad. Making it in the one pan cut down on dishes and I think gave the chicken a nicer flavour, I am not a fan of putting raw chicken in a sauce it reminds me of the soup casseroles that I don't like either.

This was very good. I browned the breasts as shown in the video. I would only tweak things a little next time. I would slice the breasts in half or pound them thinner because the best bites were the ones that had a fairly even balance of topping to chicken breast. I also had large croutons so I broke them up some before adding them to the dish, and I think it would be even better if I crushed them more next time - not completely crushed into bread crumbs, but crumbly with some chunks so it's easier to get them spread evenly over the breasts.

country:

text:
My family loves chicken parm, but I certainly do not love the work of breading and cooking the cutlets.  When we want a quick version for a weeknight dinner, I've been making just chicken baked with sauce and cheese.  So tonight I decided to try this version, and everyone gave it an enthusiastic thumbs up. I used garlic and cheese croutons, just the store brand.  It is true that after they bake and soak up some sauce, you can cut up your piece of chicken, and take a forkful of chicken plus some of the baked croutons, and you get a flavor of breaded chicken parm. So this simple addition to my quick meal worked out very well for us.  
I didn't give it the full 5 stars only because it really isn't "the real deal", and there was some unevenness in the outcome of my crouton layer - some had taken up sauce and were tasty, but others hadn't really gotten any sauce.  So to get the desired flavor you need to cut up and stir things around to mix the chicken, sauce and croutons together. 
We'll definitely make this again, and maybe with some repeat experience with it, I'll get more consistent texture throughout.

text:
Made it nearly exactly as written. I omitted the red pepper flakes because I don't like my food spicy at all. It was definitely easy...so based solely on that I'd give it a higher rating. However it was just ok. Not a bad recipe, but not one I'll make again. My husband seemed to like it but none of my three kids would eat it. I had cut my chicken into large bite sized cubes to make it easier for the kiddos to eat and to simplify serving. It baked about 40 minutes and that was plenty of time. The croutons were soggy on bottom and crispy on top, which really bugged my kids. I should have just kept the croutons off, cooked up spaghetti, then used the sauce over spaghetti and let the kids top it with the croutons. I think it would have better received.

I halved the recipe with three breasts and a 9x9 dish, but otherwise followed it exactly.  I thought the breasts I used were thick, so I baked it for 45 minutes.  The chicken was a little overdone, so I will try 35 next time.  A whole breast is too big for one serving, so I will also cut them into large chunks.  I used Texas Toast garlic croutons, and they were really good, but I will crush them a little next time.  I used Newman's Own Tomato and Basil, which was awesome.  Real parmesan chicken is a lot of work for a novice like me, so this is an easy way to get a similar flavor and texture.
